## Section 001: Tauri Executable Reference Maps
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names a maps theme without stating that its subject is routing discipline, choosing which Tauri reference to read, in what order, for which work mode, before spending any reading budget
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because reference corpora fail at the routing step, since an agent that opens the wrong document reads diligently and still plans the wrong boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing advice cannot help when the corpus lacks a document for the task at hand, and pretending a route exists is worse than naming the gap
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference governs which Tauri document to read and when, not the content of those documents, and it presumes the routed files still exist at their mapped paths
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state up front that the theme is read-order routing across the Tauri specs playbook, doctrine, and conventions files keyed by work mode and task type
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a routing map is the cheapest document in the corpus to maintain and the most expensive to get wrong, because every misroute multiplies into a misread of heavier files
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to consult the reference map before opening any heavier Tauri document, select a work mode, then follow its task-type read order
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because reference corpora fail at the routing step, since an agent that opens the wrong document reads diligently and still plans the wrong boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; routing advice cannot help when the corpus lacks a document for the task at hand, and pretending a route exists is worse than naming the gap
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference governs which Tauri document to read and when, not the content of those documents, and it presumes the routed files still exist at their mapped paths
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: state up front that the theme is read-order routing across the Tauri specs playbook, doctrine, and conventions files keyed by work mode and task type
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Reference Maps", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a routing map is the cheapest document in the corpus to maintain and the most expensive to get wrong, because every misroute multiplies into a misread of heavier files

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed map lists three local paths and three public URLs under uniform fact labels without noting that two of the local files are byte-identical duplicates or that no external retrieval is recorded
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because provenance rows steer trust, and a duplicate pair presented as two independent sources manufactures false corroboration for every claim they share
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the table cannot certify freshness, since a recorded path proves existence at mapping time, not that content still matches what Tauri 2 currently ships
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the map assigns provenance for this document's claims only and does not rank the sources or promise the archive contains no further Tauri routing material
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to record that the legacy and unclassified references are identical duplicates and that the three external rows carry no retrieval date
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that counting sources without deduplicating them inflates apparent evidence, so an honest map must state identity relations between its own rows
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat the codex-skills reference map as the routing source, the merged specs reference as its single content companion, and the external URLs as unrefreshed candidates

- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: record that the legacy and unclassified references are identical duplicates and that the three external rows carry no retrieval date

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists three corpus-hygiene failures and omits the routing failures this theme exists to prevent, skipping the map, reading files in habit order, following a stale route, and mode misclassification
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because anti-patterns pay off at triage, and a reviewer armed only with hygiene rows will approve a session that read the wrong documents thoroughly
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rows too abstract to match a live session log detect nothing, and a replacement pattern that merely negates the failure gives no action
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry covers routing and reading failures for this theme, not Tauri code anti-patterns, which the merged reference's own anti-pattern list owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add map-skipping, habit-order reading, stale-route following, and mode-misclassification rows each with a detection signal readable from a session journal
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a registry is the file's immune memory, and unencoded failures get rediscovered at the most expensive moment
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to extend the registry with the four routing failures and detect each from journal evidence, which files were opened, in what order, under which claimed mode

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names one repository verifier for editing this file and stays silent about how to verify that a routing decision itself was correct or that the routed documents still exist
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a gate that checks only document form trains agents to treat well-formed markdown as correct routing, while routes silently dangle when files move
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: no command can prove a mode classification was right, so the gate must pair mechanical checks with a recorded human judgment
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: gates verify this document and its routes, not the Tauri work products, whose gates the merged reference's cargo command block defines
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a route-resolution check that every mapped path exists and a journal check that mode, order followed, and deviations were recorded
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the cheapest high-value gate for a routing document is a link checker, because dangling routes are its dominant decay mode

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table keys adopt, adapt, and avoid to generic evidence agreement instead of the properties that govern routing value, task classifiability, corpus familiarity, and reading budget
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the routing discipline pays when the task classifies cleanly and the corpus is unfamiliar, and it costs when the agent already knows exactly which section it needs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: avoid becomes the habitual route for unfamiliar corpora, which is precisely where skipping the map costs most
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide ranks routing-discipline choices for this theme and cannot authorize skipping the security or review reading the routed documents demand
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rekey adopt to unfamiliar-corpus or ambiguous-mode tasks, adapt to partial orders for well-known tasks, and avoid to single-lookup errands with the target section already known

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model imports a one-crate, hundred-symbol boundary from generic Rust guidance and truncates its own source-pressure cell, without deriving limits from what bounds routing work, modes straddled and files held in context at once
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the binding constraint on a routing session is comprehension across ordered documents, since each added mode multiplies the sections an agent must hold while synthesizing
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: symbol counts are honored while a session straddles three modes and six documents, exactly the overload the model should catch
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds one routing-and-reading slice and says nothing about the implementation workload the routed documents govern
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rederive boundaries from modes straddled, files opened, and doctrine patterns consulted per session, and repair the truncated heading-signal cell
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that routing work scales by junctions taken, not lines written, and a model counting symbols will approve exactly the multi-mode sprawl it should split
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to hold one primary mode plus at most one secondary per session, split tasks that demand three modes, and journal the split boundary
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the binding constraint on a routing session is comprehension across ordered documents, since each added mode multiplies the sections an agent must hold while synthesizing

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the model bounds one routing-and-reading slice and says nothing about the implementation workload the routed documents govern
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: rederive boundaries from modes straddled, files opened, and doctrine patterns consulted per session, and repair the truncated heading-signal cell
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies routing work scales by junctions taken, not lines written, and a model counting symbols will approve exactly the multi-mode sprawl it should split

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify failure causes and cap retries sensibly but never say what retry means for routing, reclassify the mode once, re-resolve the route once, then escalate rather than looping
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing retries are cheap and bounded, one reclassification and one re-resolution, so unbounded rerouting signals a corpus gap rather than a transient failure
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a task that fits no mode after one honest reclassification will not fit after five, and looping burns the session budget the map exists to protect
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retry of routing and reading steps, not retries inside the Tauri work the routed documents plan
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add routing-specific retry semantics, one mode reclassification, one route re-resolution, then escalation with the journal attached
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure for a junction means refusing to send traffic down unverified routes, halting reading when resolution fails rather than improvising a path

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement names multi-system spans and SLO-bearing traffic as limits but gives no early indicators that the routing scheme itself is outgrowing five modes and eight task types
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing schemes fail by accretion, since each new task type stretches an existing mode until classifications become coin flips, and leading indicators buy response time hard limits cannot
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: limits read as targets invite corpus sprawl, and a boundary detected at the boundary has already been crossed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the boundaries bound this routing reference, not the scaling of applications the routed documents plan
